fill-rule="evenodd"></path></svg></span></a></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="mb-md gray-dark font--subhead font-xxs" data-qa="timestamp"><div class="display-date">October 12, 2019 at 9:18 AM EDT</div></div><div class="article-body"><div class="teaser-content"><section><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">President Trump told reporters Friday that he didn’t know whether Rudy Giuliani was still his personal attorney, adding that the two hadn’t spoken since Thursday.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“I don’t know,” Trump said, <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GatxskMEEkU">responding</a> to a question about the lawyer as he prepared to leave the White House for a rally in Louisiana Friday evening. “I haven’t spoken to Rudy. I spoke to him yesterday briefly. He’s a very good attorney, and he has been my attorney.”</p></div></section></div><div class="remainder-content"><section><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In a text message to The Washington Post’s Josh Dawsey shortly after the president’s comments, Giuliani confirmed that he’s still representing Trump.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Yes,” Giuliani wrote. “I am still his attorney.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Also Friday, U.S. Ambassador to the European Union Gordon Sondland, a key figure in the Ukraine controversy, bucked the State Department and announced he would appear before House investigators under subpoena next week.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The State Department blocked Sondland last week from appearing before three panels focused on Trump’s efforts to press Ukrainian President Volodymyr Zelensky to investigate former vice president Joe Biden and his son Hunter Biden at a time when U.S. military aid to Ukraine was being withheld.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">And House Democrats moved forward with closed-door testimony from Marie Yovanovitch, the former U.S. ambassador to Ukraine. In opening remarks, Yovanovitch, who is appearing under subpoena, said her abrupt departure in May came as <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/national-security/ousted-ukraine-envoy-marie-yovanovitch-expected-to-testify-in-impeachment-inquiry-today/2019/10/11/d571830e-eba0-11e9-85c0-85a098e47b37_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_10">a direct result of pressure</a> Trump placed on the State Department to remove her.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">● At least four national security officials <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/national-security/at-least-four-national-security-officials-raised-alarms-about-ukraine-policy-before-and-after-trump-call-with-ukrainian-president/2019/10/10/ffe0c88a-eb6d-11e9-9c6d-436a0df4f31d_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_11">raised alarms about Ukraine policy</a> before and after Trump’s call with the Ukrainian president.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_2"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">● White House political appointees <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/national-security/white-house-political-appointees-overrode-career-staffers-before-freezing-ukraine-aid/2019/10/10/e27435e2-eba0-11e9-85c0-85a098e47b37_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_13">overrode career staffers</a> before freezing Ukraine aid.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_2"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">● Two business associates of Giuliani <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/two-business-associates-of-trumps-personal-lawyer-giuliani-have-been-arrested-and-are-in-custody/2019/10/10/9f9c101a-eb63-11e9-9306-47cb0324fd44_story.html?hpid=hp_hp-top-table-main_giuliani-1011a%3Ahomepage%2Fstory-ans&amp;tid=lk_inline_manual_15">were arrested at the airport</a> as they tried to leave the United States.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/context/read-the-whistleblower-complaint-regarding-president-trump-s-communications-with-ukrainian-president-volodymyr-zelensky/4b9e0ca5-3824-467f-b1a3-77f2d4ee16aa/?tid=lk_inline_manual_16" title="www.washingtonpost.com">The whistleblower complaint </a>| <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/context/official-readout-president-trump-s-july-25-phone-call-with-ukraine-s-volodymyr-zelensky/4b228f51-17e7-45bc-b16c-3b2643f3fbe0/?tid=lk_inline_manual_16" title="www.washingtonpost.com">The rough transcript of Trump’s call with Zelensky</a> |<a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/context/letter-from-white-house-counsel-pat-cipollone-to-house-leaders/0e1845e5-5c19-4e7a-ab4b-9d591a5fda7b/?tid=lk_inline_manual_16">The letter from White House counsel to House leaders</a></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>9:55 p.m.: Trump tells Louisiana crowd that Pelosi ‘hates’ the United States</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In the hours after the former U.S. ambassador <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/national-security/ousted-ukraine-envoy-marie-yovanovitch-expected-to-testify-in-impeachment-inquiry-today/2019/10/11/d571830e-eba0-11e9-85c0-85a098e47b37_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_19">testified</a> that Trump pressured the State Department to oust her and House Democrats vowed to press on with their impeachment inquiry, the president took the stage in Lake Charles, La. — the roaring crowd a far cry from the drumbeat of investigations in Washington.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_3"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Trump began the rally — his second in two days — with a familiar harangue against Democrats, comparing the inquiry to a “nonstop battle to overturn your vote.” But when he singled out Pelosi, he escalated his attacks, calling her “Nervous Nancy” and crudely pantomiming her mannerisms. He said her support of the investigation means she “hates the country.”</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_3"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Nancy Pelosi hates the United States of America,” he repeated. </p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">His comments come the day after his Minneapolis rally, when Trump leveled some of his most personal attacks yet against Biden and his family, mixing curse words with unsubstantiated claims.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Earlier Friday, Pelosi told Democratic lawmakers in a conference call that Trump’s rhetoric had become “beyond disgraceful.”</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_4"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“POTUS has become a potty-mouth, and children are listening,” she said, according to a Democratic aide who took notes on the call. </p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">At the rally, Trump deployed more profanity in talking about the impeachment inquiry. As he spoke, the newest Little League World Series champions, hailing from Louisiana, watched from the stands.</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>8:30 p.m.: Yovanovitch finishes all-day deposition, as Democrats praise her decision to come forward and Republicans blast the closed-door process</b></p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_4"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">After nine hours of questioning on Capitol Hill, Yovanovitch left the closed-door deposition at 7:40, accompanied by her lawyers.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Democrats praised the former ambassador for complying with their subpoena and sitting for the lengthy interview. On a conference call with House Democrats, Intelligence Committee Chairman Adam B. Schiff (D-Calif.) called her act courageous.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_5"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“She has had a distinguished career where she demonstrated great courage, and she may be demonstrating her greatest moment of courage right now,” Schiff said, according to a member who spoke on the condition of anonymity to discuss the private conversation.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Rep. Tom Malinowski (D-N.J.) said in an interview with CNN that Yovanovitch’s example could prompt other officials to come forward, too. </p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“There are a lot of folks at the State Department, the [National Security Council] and throughout the United States government who will see this as a good example, that it can be done,” he said.</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_5"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Republican lawmakers, however, blasted Democrats — particularly Schiff — for presiding over a secretive process that they said was unfair to the president. </p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_6"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“For goodness sake, now we’ve got almost 20 hours of testimony from two ambassadors, and the American people don’t know what happened in those closed-door sessions, other than what the majority has selectively cherry-picked and leaked out,” said Rep. Jim Jordan (R-Ohio), the top Republican on the House Oversight and Reform Committee.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Jordan and other Republicans refrained from commenting on Yovanovitch’s testimony, citing the classified nature of the proceedings, while also claiming that nothing in her testimony warranted such secrecy.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">They would not, for instance, say whether they accepted her denial — made in a publicly released opening statement — that she ever spoke ill of Trump, an allegation that circulated widely in conservative circles and appears to have contributed to the decision to recall her. </p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_6"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_7"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Instead, they lambasted the process and the Democrats running it. Rep. Lee Zeldin (R-N.Y.) called for allowing Trump’s counsel to be present and to be able to cross examine witnesses, as well as for Republicans to be afforded subpoena power. </p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“How about the Democrats provide the Republicans and the president the same exact rights that they would demand if everything was reversed?” he said.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Jordan also called for the unmasking of the anonymous CIA whistleblower whose complaint sparked the impeachment probe, amplifying calls from Trump that have been renounced by some Republicans.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Why don’t we know who this whistleblower is?” he said. “They deserve protection, but ... they’re not entitled to anonymity.”</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns db dn-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_mob_bigbox_8"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Mike DeBonis</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>6:30 p.m.: Pelosi tells lawmakers to keep impeachment inquiry focused on Ukraine, calls Trump a ‘potty mouth’</b></p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_7"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Pelosi told House Democrats on Friday evening that they should resist the urge to expand their ongoing impeachment investigation and stay focused on Trump’s conduct in Ukraine — even as the president ramps up his rhetoric and new allegations emerge about his dealings with China and Turkey.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“There are a lot of rabbit holes to go down here, but we need to resist that temptation,” one member said, describing Pelosi’s comment. “Keep it clear in a way that is easy to communicate to folks.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">That lawmaker and others described the hour-plus caucus conference call on the condition of anonymity to discuss a private conversation.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Another member echoed that account, saying that Pelosi indicated some of their ancillary findings could merit investigation, but “the Ukraine issue and abuse of power is not only the most egregious act, but it’s an act he already admitted to and has the additional virtue of being easily understood by the public.”</p></div><div><div class="cb bg-offwhite mt-xxs pad-top-md pad-bottom-md mb-lg ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns dn db-ns relative" style="min-height:250px"><div class="absolute z-0" style="left:50%;top:50%">AD</div><div class="relative z-1"><div class=""><wp-ad class="hide-for-print hide-for-print" id="slug_inline_bb_8"></wp-ad></div></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Pelosi was also asked what the House could do to enforce its subpoenas, which the White House has indicated it will ignore. One member said Pelosi signaled she “would be willing to do what was necessary.” She acknowledged that some lawmakers have suggested using the House Sergeant at Arms “to round up witnesses,” neither endorsing nor dismissing the idea, according to a senior Democratic aide, but saying she’d leave the decision up to the relevant committees. </p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The speaker  then criticized Trump’s recent public statements — particularly about Biden and his other potential Democratic opponents — saying they’ve become especially acerbic.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“POTUS has become a potty mouth, and children are listening,” she said, according to an aide’s notes on the call. “This is beyond disgraceful.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">She instructed her caucus to ignore his rhetoric, which she said was purely politically motivated. </p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“What we are doing on impeachment is about the facts — ‘Just the facts, ma’am’ — and the Constitution,” Pelosi said. “His policy, his personality, his potty mouth, that’s about the election and let’s make sure that we understand the reasons he is — the inquiry is because he has not honored his oath of office. We will honor ours.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Mike DeBonis</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>5:15 p.m.: Trump, when asked if Giuliani is still his attorney, says ‘I don’t know’</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Trump told reporters Friday that he didn’t know whether Giuliani was still his personal attorney, adding that the two hadn’t spoken since Thursday.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Well, I don’t know,” Trump said, <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GatxskMEEkU">responding</a> to a question about the lawyer as he prepared to leave the White House for a rally in Louisiana. “I haven’t spoken to Rudy. I spoke to him yesterday briefly. He’s a very good attorney, and he has been my attorney.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Trump then added, “Yeah, sure,” before moving on to another question. </p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In a text message to The Washington Post’s Josh Dawsey shortly after the president’s comments, Giuliani confirmed that he’s still representing Trump. </p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Yes,” Giuliani wrote. “I am still his attorney.”</p></div><div><div class="" data-oembed-type="twitter"><blockquote class="twitter-tweet"><p dir="ltr" lang="en">"I am still his attorney," Giuliani says, when asked again by text message. <a href="https://t.co/Qi0pTvYAvV">https://t.co/Qi0pTvYAvV</a></p>— Josh Dawsey (@jdawsey1) <a href="https://twitter.com/jdawsey1/status/1182767547411767296?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">October 11, 2019</a></blockquote>
<script async="" charset="utf-8" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js"></script>
</div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In messages to New York Magazine’s Olivia Nuzzi, Giuliani offered two “thumbs up” reactions to Nuzzi’s questions about Trump’s statement, before <a href="https://twitter.com/Olivianuzzi/status/1182768879505956864">reportedly telling her</a>, “I spoke to him yesterday and I have no reason to believe I’m not.”</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>2:10 p.m.: Yovanovitch appeared under a subpoena </b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">House investigators say they issued a subpoena to compel the appearance of Yovanovitch after learning Thursday night that the State Department had directed her not to appear Friday for a voluntary interview.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“This is the latest example of the Administration’s efforts to conceal the facts from the American people and obstruct our lawful and constitutionally-authorized impeachment inquiry,” three Democratic chairmen said in a joint statement. “As is required of her, the Ambassador is now complying with the subpoena and answering questions from both Democratic and Republican Members and staff.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In the statement, the chairmen also renewed a warning to the White House that preventing witness cooperation “will be deemed obstruction of a co-equal branch of government and an adverse inference may be drawn against the President on the underlying allegations of corruption and coverup.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The statement came from Intelligence Committee Chairman Adam B. Schiff (D-Calif.), House Oversight and Reform Committee Chairman Elijah E. Cummings (D-Md.) and House Foreign Affairs Committee Chairman Eliot L. Engel (D-N.Y.).</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>2 p.m.: White House talking points suggest a ‘serious danger’ Yovanovitch will reveal information without authorization</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In talking points distributed to Republican lawmakers on Capitol Hill, the White House suggested arguing that Yovanovitch is in a “precarious position” because she is appearing for her deposition without State Department lawyers.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“We are not concerned with any information Yovanovitch might share, because the President did nothing wrong,” the talking points say. “But we are concerned that Schiff is putting her a precarious position by having her testify in secret without State Department lawyers be present. </p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Only State Department lawyers would be able to provide Yovanovitch with the correct counsel on what is classified or privileged and without that counsel there is serious danger that she could breach her obligations as a current employee not to reveal such information without authorization.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">While Yovanovitch was recalled from her post in Ukraine in May, she remains a State Department employee.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The White House talking points, which were shared by a Republican official, also suggest saying that Schiff is not only acting in complete disregard of Yovanovitch, he is furthering a “sham show trial that no one should seek to participate in.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“By throwing those protections out the window, Rep. Schiff has shown the world that he is willing to ride roughshod over fair process and to use career officials to further a baseless political objective without any regard for the officials themselves,” the talking points say.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">— <i>Rachael Bade</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>12:45 p.m.: Pelosi vows Trump ‘will be held accountable’</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In a letter to House Democrats ahead of a planned conference call Friday, Pelosi touted “increased outside validation of our efforts” and thanked colleagues for their “seriousness of purpose” during the impeachment inquiry.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“The President’s actions threaten our national security, violate our Constitution and undermine the integrity of our elections,” Pelosi wrote to fellow Democrats. “No one is above the law. The President will be held accountable.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Pelosi pointed to a <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/local/legal-issues/appeals-court-rules-against-trump-in-fight-with-congress-over-presidents-accounting-firm-records/2019/10/11/42933894-b9ea-11e9-b3b4-2bb69e8c4e39_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_94">court ruling Friday</a> as validation of the oversight authority of Congress, which the Trump administration has been resisting. The federal appeals court ruling rejected Trump’s bid to block a House panel from subpoenaing business records from his accounting firm.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Pelosi also pointed to a statement this week by 17 former Watergate special prosecutors supportive of the impeachment inquiry, as well as another from conservative lawyers from past Republican administrations.</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>12:10 p.m.: Trump highlights previous effort to impeach him that failed badly</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In late-morning tweets and retweets, Trump returned to taunting “Do Nothing Democrats” and House Intelligence Committee Chairman Adam B. Schiff (D-Calif.) and also highlighted a previous effort to impeach him that failed badly.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">As House investigators were hearing testimony behind closed doors on Capitol Hill, Trump shared <a href="https://hannity.com/media-room/flashback-to-dec-2017-58-dems-vote-to-impeach-trump-for-criticizing-nfl-anthem-protesters/">a blog post</a> by Fox News host Sean Hannity headlined “Flashback to DEC 2017: 58 Dems Vote to Impeach Trump for Criticizing NFL Anthem Protesters.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Hannity was referring to a December 2017 vote forced by Rep. Al Green (D-Tex.), who introduced articles of impeachment describing Trump as a bigot who incites hate.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Green’s articles of impeachment cited Trump’s repeated criticism of mostly African American NFL players who knelt during the national anthem as a form of protest against abuse by police officers.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The articles of impeachment also included references to Trump’s remarks in the aftermath of a deadly white supremacist rally in Charlottesville and his attacks on Rep. Frederica S. Wilson (D-Fla.), an African American lawmaker.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">House Speaker Nancy Pelosi (D-Calif.) opposed Green’s measure, which was blocked by a vote of 364 to 58.</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>12 p.m.: Yovanovitch tells Congress Trump pressured State Dept. to remove her</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The former U.S. ambassador to Ukraine whose abrupt ouster in May has become a topic of interest for House impeachment investigators said Friday that her departure came as a direct result of pressure Trump placed on the State Department to remove her, according to her <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/context/read-marie-yovanovitch-s-prepared-deposition-statement/dffbf543-a373-46e0-a957-bc12a9371af4/?tid=lk_inline_manual_106">prepared remarks before Congress</a> obtained by The Washington Post.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Yovanovitch told lawmakers that she was forced to leave Kiev on “the next plane” in the spring and subsequently removed from her post, with the State Department’s No. 2 official telling her that, though she had done nothing wrong, the president had lost confidence in her, and that the State Department had been under significant pressure to remove her since the summer of 2018.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In explaining her departure, she acknowledged months of criticisms by President Trump’s personal lawyer Rudolph W. Giuliani, who had accused her of privately badmouthing the president and seeking to protect the interests of Biden and his son who served on the board of a Ukrainian energy company.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Yovanovitch denied those allegations and said she was “incredulous” that her superiors decided to remove her based on “unfounded and false claims by people with clearly questionable motives.” </p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Read more <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/national-security/ousted-ukraine-envoy-marie-yovanovitch-expected-to-testify-in-impeachment-inquiry-today/2019/10/11/d571830e-eba0-11e9-85c0-85a098e47b37_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_110">here</a>.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Karoun Demirjian, John Hudson and Paul Sonne</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>11:40 a.m.: Cummings hails court ruling as ‘resounding victory for Congressional oversight’</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">House Oversight and Reform Committee Chairman Elijah E. Cummings hailed a court ruling Friday related to Trump’s business records as “a fundamental and resounding victory for Congressional oversight, our Constitutional system of checks and balances, and the rule of law.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The Maryland Democrat issued a statement following a 2-1 <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/local/legal-issues/appeals-court-rules-against-trump-in-fight-with-congress-over-presidents-accounting-firm-records/2019/10/11/42933894-b9ea-11e9-b3b4-2bb69e8c4e39_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_115">ruling by the U.S. Court of Appeals for the D.C. Circuit</a> that allows Congress to seek eight years of Trump’s business records from his accounting firm Mazars.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“For far too long, the President has placed his personal interests over the interests of the American people,” Cummings said. “After months of delay, it is time for the President to stop blocking Mazars from complying with the Committee’s lawful subpoena. We must fulfill our stated legislative and oversight objectives and permit the American people to obtain answers about some of the deeply troubling questions regarding the President’s adherence to Constitutional and statutory requirements to avoid conflicts of interest.”</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>10:45 a.m.: Appeals court rules against Trump in fight with Congress over president’s accounting firm records</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Congress can seek eight years of Trump’s business records from his accounting firm, a federal appeals court in Washington ruled Friday in one of several legal battles over access to the president’s financial data.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In a 2-1 ruling, the U.S. Court of Appeals for the D.C. Circuit upheld Congress’s broad investigative powers and rejected the president’s bid to block lawmakers from subpoenaing the documents.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The case is one of several clashes between the Democrat-controlled House and the Republican president over Trump’s data that is expected to reach the Supreme Court. In this case, the judges ruled that Trump’s arguments — that the subpoenas were invalid because Congress lacked a “legitimate legislative purpose” for its subpoenas — were incorrect.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Contrary to the President’s arguments, the Committee possesses authority under both the House Rules and the Constitution to issue the subpoena, and Mazars [Trump’s accounting firm] must comply,” Judges David S. Tatel and Patricia A. Millett wrote for the court. Both were appointed by Democratic presidents.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Read more <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/politics/wp/2019/10/11/congress-may-seek-8-years-of-trumps-business-records-from-his-accounting-firm-appeals-court-rules/?tid=lk_inline_manual_123">here</a>.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Ann E. Marimow, Spencer S. Hsu and David A. Fahrenthold</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>10:40 a.m.: </b>
<b>Trump obfuscates, misleads and exaggerates to make his case against impeachment</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Trump’s propensity to mislead, misconstrue and obfuscate is escalating as he confronts the threat of becoming just the third president in U.S. history to be impeached.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">For days, Trump and his allies have repeatedly charged that the whistleblower — whose complaint about Trump’s call with the president of Ukraine set off the current impeachment inquiry — made up a “false story,” even though many of the claims have been shown to be accurate. The president has insisted that his top Democratic and Republican critics on Capitol Hill should be impeached for their efforts against him, despite a centuries-old precedent that prevents such an action.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">And White House lawyers this week sent congressional leaders an eight-page letter vowing not to cooperate with the House Democrats’ impeachment inquiry that was laden with imprecise or misleading interpretations of congressional oversight powers and the chamber’s constitutional right to impeach, according to legal experts.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Read more <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trump-obfuscates-misleads-and-exaggerates-to-make-his-case-against-impeachment/2019/10/10/398d8d0a-eaa3-11e9-9c6d-436a0df4f31d_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_130">here</a>.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Seung Min Kim</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>10:30 a.m.: Maryland’s Larry Hogan becomes third GOP governor to support impeachment inquiry</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Maryland Gov. Larry Hogan is the latest Republican elected official to say he supports the Trump impeachment inquiry.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“I think we do need an inquiry because we have to get to the bottom of it,” Hogan told Margaret Hoover of PBS’s Firing Line, in an interview that was taped Thursday night and will be aired in full on Friday. “I don’t see any other way to get to the facts.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The popular two-term governor said he is “not ready” to say he supports an impeachment or a removal of the president, but thinks an inquiry of his conduct is warranted. House Democrats launched an inquiry just over two weeks ago, focusing on Trump’s pressure on the Ukrainian president to investigate Biden and his son.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Hogan joins fellow Republican Govs. Phil Scott (Vermont) and Charlie Baker (Mass.) in backing an investigation. But Hogan, who is term-limited and decided against a primary challenge to Trump earlier this year, also raised concerns about the process moving forward.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Read more <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/local/md-politics/hogan-supports-impeachment-inquiry-i-dont-see-any-other-way-to-get-to-the-facts/2019/10/11/4e8504be-ec28-11e9-85c0-85a098e47b37_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_138">here</a>.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Ovetta Wiggins</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>10:10 a.m.: Yovanovitch arrives for deposition</b></p></div><div><figure class="pad-top-xs mb-md ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns center hide-for-print"><div class="powa-wrapper"><div class="powa-skip" data-ad-bar="1" data-aspect-ratio="0.5625" data-blurb="true" data-org="wapo" data-playthrough="true" data-uuid="68631240-f167-46d3-a046-402efd47a742"></div></div></figure></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Marie Yovanovitch, the former U.S. ambassador to Ukraine, arrived at the Capitol for a scheduled closed-door deposition in front of three House committees.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">She did not answer questions from reporters as she entered the building.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Up until the time of her arrival, there was uncertainty about whether the White House or State Department would try to block her testimony.</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>8:50 a.m.: Sondland to appear for deposition next week, lawyers say</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">U.S. Ambassador to the European Union Gordon Sondland will appear for a deposition next week under subpoena in the House’s impeachment inquiry but cannot turn over documents requested by investigators, his lawyers said Friday.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The State Department blocked Sondland from appearing before the House Intelligence, Foreign Affairs and Oversight and Reform committees on Tuesday with an overnight order not to show. Democrats subsequently issued a subpoena for his testimony, and later that day the White House informed Democratic leaders they had no intention of cooperating with the investigation.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Notwithstanding the State Department’s current direction to not testify, Ambassador Sondland will honor the Committees’ subpoena, and he looks forward to testifying on Thursday,” Sondland’s lawyers said in a statement. “Ambassador Sondland has at all times acted with integrity and in the interests of the United States. He has no agenda apart from answering the Committees’ questions fully and truthfully.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The lawyers, Robert Luskin and Kwame Manley, said that State Department regulations prohibit Sondland from producing documents concerning his official responsibilities and that the department has the “sole authority” to do so.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Ambassador Sondland hopes the materials will be shared with the Committees in advance of his Thursday testimony,” they added.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Sondland was one of a handful of U.S. diplomats who facilitated Trump’s interactions with Ukrainian leaders, according to a trove of text messages that former U.S. special envoy Kurt Volker provided to House investigators last week. Messages that were released publicly show that the administration sought a promise from Ukrainian leaders to investigate the 2016 election and the energy firm, Burisma, that had paid Hunter Biden to sit on its board.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Karoun Demirjian</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>8 a.m.: Trump heading to another campaign rally on Friday night</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Trump is scheduled to leave the White House shortly after 4 p.m. and head to Lake Charles, La., where thousands of supporters are expected for another campaign rally on Friday night.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">During <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trump-attacks-bidens-in-personal-and-coarse-terms-at-minnesota-rally/2019/10/10/3c2304c2-ebc6-11e9-9c6d-436a0df4f31d_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_158">a rally Thursday night in Minneapolis</a>, Trump leveled some of his most personal attacks yet against Biden and his family, highlighting unsubstantiated claims about his potential 2020 rival’s son and using profanity to describe Biden’s tenure as vice president.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Among other things, Trump mocked Hunter Biden’s personal problems, including his discharge from the Navy after he tested positive for cocaine use.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Hunter, you know nothing about energy, you know nothing about China, you know nothing about anything, frankly,” Trump said to a near-capacity crowd. “Hunter, you’re a loser.” </p></div><div><figure class="pad-top-xs mb-md ml-neg-gutter mr-neg-gutter mr-auto-ns ml-auto-ns center hide-for-print"><div class="powa-wrapper"><div class="powa-skip" data-ad-bar="1" data-aspect-ratio="0.5625" data-blurb="true" data-org="wapo" data-playthrough="true" data-uuid="16c88c6f-4e9d-40c9-ae94-c8c27c70e8c2"></div></div></figure></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Joe Biden went on Twitter after the rally, referring to his appearance at a town hall hosted by the Human Rights Campaign and CNN on LGBTQ issues.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“I spent my night at the HRC forum talking about the fundamental respect every human being deserves,” Biden <a href="https://twitter.com/JoeBiden/status/1182504092817444865">tweeted</a>. “You spent yours showing how little respect for anyone else you have. America is so much stronger than your weakness, @realDonaldTrump.”</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Before leaving Washington on Friday afternoon, Trump is scheduled to have photos taken with Little League championship baseball and softball teams and meet with Chinese Vice Premier Han Zheng.</p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>7 a.m.: Former ambassador to Ukraine scheduled for deposition Friday morning</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Yovanovitch is expected to be deposed at 10 a.m. by House investigators Friday as part of the ongoing impeachment inquiry, despite the White House’s stated objections and refusal to cooperate with the Democratic-led proceedings.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Yovanovitch was confirmed as ambassador to Ukraine in August 2016, but recalled in May, after conservative activists — including Giuliani — accused her of being biased against Trump. State Department officials have said the accusations against the career diplomat are baseless.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">She is one of several current and former diplomats that the House Intelligence, Foreign Affairs and Oversight committees have identified as witnesses in their probe into whether Trump pressured Ukraine’s president to investigate his political rivals.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The panels have issued subpoenas to the White House, Giuliani and two business associates, and several Cabinet-level officials, including Secretary of State Mike Pompeo, Secretary of Energy Rick Perry, Defense Secretary Mark T. Esper and the acting director of the Office of Management and Budget, Russell T. Vought, requesting materials related to the administration’s interactions with Ukraine. </p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">But to date, the panels have recorded only one deposition — with former special U.S. envoy to Ukraine Kurt Volker, who quit his post hours after he was requested to appear for a deposition.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Read more <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/national-security/ousted-ukraine-envoy-marie-yovanovitch-expected-to-testify-in-impeachment-inquiry-today/2019/10/11/d571830e-eba0-11e9-85c0-85a098e47b37_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_172">here</a>.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Karoun Demirjian </i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>6:45 a.m.: New revelations about Trump test Pelosi’s narrow impeachment strategy</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Recent revelations about Trump’s conduct are testing the limits of House Speaker Nancy Pelosi’s narrow impeachment strategy, leading some Democrats to wonder whether the probe should be expanded beyond the Ukraine scandal.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Since House Democrats launched their impeachment inquiry just over two weeks ago, Pelosi (D-Calif.) and her top lieutenants have coalesced around a plan to focus on Trump’s pressure on the Ukrainian president to investigate Biden, a 2020 presidential candidate, and his son Hunter. </p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">The episode, Democrats argue, is clear-cut, easy for Americans to understand and doesn’t require further proof as the White House has released a rough transcript of the call.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">But a spate of allegations about other possible abuses have led some Democrats to rethink the strategy.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">Read more <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/new-revelations-about-trump-test-pelosis-narrow-impeachment-strategy/2019/10/10/cac7e24c-eb85-11e9-bafb-da248f8d5734_story.html?tid=lk_inline_manual_180">here</a>.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><i>— Rachael Bade</i></p></div><div><div><div><hr style="margin-top:-10px;margin-bottom:-10px;"/></div></div></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined"><b>6:40 a.m.: George Conway takes shot at Giuliani</b></p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">George Conway, the conservative lawyer and spouse of White House counselor Kellyanne Conway, took a shot at Giuliani on Friday, referring to the arrests this week of two of his associates on charges they schemed to funnel foreign money to U.S. politicians while trying to influence U.S.-Ukraine relations.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">“Rudy 1986 would have indicted Rudy 2019 in a New York minute,” Conway <a href="https://twitter.com/gtconway3d/status/1182607012502347776">tweeted</a>.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">In 1986, Giuliani was a federal prosecutor, serving as U.S. attorney for the Southern District of New York.</p></div><div><p class="font--body font-copy color-gray-darkest ma-0 pad-bottom-md undefined">His two associates, Lev Parnas and Igor Fruman, who had been helping Giuliani investigate Biden, were arrested Wednesday evening at Dulles International Airport outside Washington, where they had one-way tickets on a flight out of the country, officials said.</p></div></section></div></div><div
